‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§¶‡§Ç‡§∂‡§®‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç‡•• ‡•¨‡•® ‡••

‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§É ‚Äî‡§® ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É‡•• ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡•§

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ï‡§≤‡§§‡§æ‡§ó‡•É-‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡•ã‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§ü‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß-‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§® ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≤‡§≠‡•á‡§§ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§É ‚Äî‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡•§

to seat herself audaciously on the shoulders of her master holding and controlling the reins. The horse proceeded a short distance, pacing as directed by her ; then it dealt kicks and fled fast away from all control jumping and biting to the woods.

Vidhushaka.‚Äî I do not understand the meaning of these words. Is not the King in the woman’s apartments of the palace.

Manthara.‚Äî You had better search for your friend everywhere up to all the boundaries of the palace, the courtyard square, the temples, the storied porticos, arbours, harems and everywhere in corners ; similarly indoors outdoors, sidedoors, and inside too ; up on the loft, beneath the pavements and even in the rat holes ; you will not find the king.
Vidhushaka.‚Äî What is the cause of departure ?

‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡•• ‡•¨‡•© ‡••

‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§É‚Äî‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§™‡•Ä-‡§∑‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§É ‚Äî‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§ø‡•§

Manthara.‚Äî A person abandons the house he dislikes, when it is visited by an owl. So does he, one infested with bugs. Why not then, a house infested by an accursed wife ?
Vidhushaka.‚Äî Give up fun. His worship was deep in love with Suruchi, was he not ? Why this hurried departure ?
Manthara.‚Äî This news was learnt by me from the mouth of Suruchi that His Majesty becoming somewhat indifferent to worldly pleasures and neglecting even her lady-ship a little went to the forest to worship Hari for the blessing of a son.
Vidhushaka.‚Äî Wonderful ! I never knew this matter before.

Manthara.‚Äî Does not his majesty stir about without your approval ?
Vidhushaka:‚Äî Alas ! Time has so radically changed that it has converted the king into an ascetic. Indeed I will marry a couple of wives to become a recluse.

[Exeunt.

ACT II.
SCENE I.
Before the Palace on a meadow.

Enter Sumati, Purohit, Bard and other citizens.

Sumati.‚Äî From the lord, who has bathed in conclusion of the penances, a despatch has come,

that he is returning (home) and will gracefully condescend to resume his own office. Let all good citizens be ready to receive him in the regular gradation of caste and order ; and likewise, the military paraphernalia and courtesans of lovely eyes with waterfilled vessels of gold.
Commander-in-chief.‚Äî All are ready. Filled with enthusiasm at the news of His Majesty’s (expected) return the king’s servants and subjects adorned in suitable jewelry and clothing are standing in groups in various places in the decorated street. Even immoveables, plantations, moveables and animals appear seized with fervour.

fumes are adorned in green garments consisting of fine new turf.
The young deer with parts of young grass chewed, playing about with an ecstasy of bounds, offer to the king a hearty welcome, by means of side-glances with curved necks. The flowing river singing away by a gentle drop on the stones of the bed, softly invites the honoured king by the babblings of the current. Learning from Aruna’s word, of the intended arrival of our lord, the sun has hurried himself (to appear at the scene) liberated from the bondage of the sea and the night. (Behind the scenes) May you be victorious O! King ; obtaining the gem of a son do guard the realm till the moon and stars endure.

(The screen lifted, Enter King with a mango fruit in hand).

King.‚Äî I greet all.
All.‚Äî Triumph O ! King.
Bard.‚Äî May victory attend you, a bee in the foot of Lakshmi’s Lord ; sovereign supreme commanding the homage of emperors anointed as rulers of the sea-girt Earth ; served by officers from the premier downwards, the legislative and executive ministers, the chief justice and so forth, luminaries of intellect belittling Brihaspati himself ; the president of a court filled with learned men eminent in the knowledge of the scriptures ris. the Vedas and their commentaries ; possessing a perfect organisation of sovereignty riz. ministers, advisers, treasury, a realm, forts and an army in completeness, one who has subdued the world by the state-craft of dip-

lomacy, charity, differentiation and punishment, to whom allegiance and tribute are paid from the ends of the Earth (from all quarters of the globe), armed with bows, whose wooden and metallic arrows successfully hit the eye-pupils of flies ; who conveys a convulsive tremor into the pregnant wombs of the enemy’s women, who is mounted on gold or ruby thrones, surrounded by royal insignia ? the umbrellas and chamaras : and who has now secured a blessing by service at the foot of the Garuda-riding-lord Vishnu. To you all the subjects here assembled, offer an address of welcome.
King.‚Äî I am thankful to all. Let the citizens sit down.
Sumati.‚Äî Your majestyall are eager to hear how your majesty’s endeavour bore fruit ; May it please your majesty.

King.‚ÄîSumati, even now I am stricken sad. Alas, having worshipped the great and faultless Hari of perfect attributes in a dense jungle for 2 years by means of incessant and severe austerities and then attaining a vision of Sreenath, the fountain of blessings, the infinite one of smiling face capable of conferring the moksha itself, I regret that I begged him, O ! Sumati, only for a son instead of final emancipation from mortal existence.
Sumati.‚Äî After laying by, a store of piety and merit, through the instrumentality of an eminently righteous son, the qualification for moksha will follow.
King.‚Äî He, an ocean of grace, said, in words of deep resonance, with sympathy and tenderness,

(‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É)

“you better pluck one fruit from that good mango tree‚Äù. I gathered a large number of fruits out of eagerness, to get a number of sons. On the way, I found the fruits transformed into one. Here it is, got by the grace of the Lord. The Lord’s will is clear ‚Äî that I should have but a single son.
All.‚Äî It is certain that this being a boon obtained from the grace of the everlasting one, it will be fruitful of enduring results.
King‚Äî Friend, this should be caused to be delivered to my most beloved queen Suruchi.
Sumati.‚Äî As your majesty commands.
King.‚Äî The cheeks (sides) of the fruit should not be cut. Let her be told that the whole should be eaten.

(Exit Sumati taking the fruit.)

In the midst of this assembly. no one remembers Suneeti, the anointed senior queen who is living in the forest. What is the good of the King’s austerities, entangled as he is in the meshes of a wife.

Suruchi.‚Äî Let alone that old story (of the puranas) ; what is to be done now ? In the absence of both let a son at least be got, though a less welcome alternative ; friend, as it is very stout, I am unable to eat it all ; you better eat a half.
Manthara.‚ÄîTormented by numerous sons filling a whole house, I suffer like a corpse preyed on by vultures. I want no more issue. However this is indeed an easy device for lineage. I am sorry that this device was not

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ó‡§∞‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡•• ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§´‡§≤‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Ä‡§ú‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‚Äî ‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî(‡§à‡§∑‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§π‡§≤‡•á ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‚Äî‡§µ‡§∞‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ú‡•Å‡§ó‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡•á‡•§ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§®‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§ø‡•§

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‚Äî‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§

known to me or my husband before : madam, if the whole be not palatable, let a portion be sent to Suneeti.
Suruchi.‚Äî I will send poison to her. Let it be given (to me) the juice being squeezed out from the seed.
Manthara.‚Äî (does as told).
Suruchi.‚Äî (tasting a little), Friend, being old. it appears somewhat sour ; mix sugar.
Manthara.‚Äî The fruit of divine gift should not be eaten with disgust.
Suruchi.‚Äî I am not very particular about lineage. Now that I have no issue at present, how am I any the worse for it.
Manthara.‚Äî Here it is, mixed with sugar. Let it be eaten.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî(‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø)‡•§

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ** ‚Äî‡§´‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§É‡•§

‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§π‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•ã‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç
‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡§Ç‡•§
‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡•á‡§§‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç‡•• ‡•≠‡•© ‡••

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§É ‡••

Suruchi.‚Äî (does as told)
Manthara.‚Äî I presume that hereafter there is no need for marriage inasmuch as the birth of issue is vouchsafed by mere fruit-eating.
Suruchi.‚Äî Simpleton. Is the perpetuation of lineage the only object of marriage ? There is a flood of inexpressible sensations in youth when the features suddenly assume a glow ; the hair standing on end, delirious joy, thoughts of love, and an ever throbbing heart, besides a special skill of the shrewd eyes in a new language of signs : cupid is the creator of a new world for those who are subject to emotion.

End of Scene II.

Scene III.
In the forest.
Enter Sumati and servant with a plate of flowers and fruits.

Sumati.‚Äî (To himself)

Sister Suneeti was born as a boon of God, in a mansion resembling the palace of Indra. She grew up fondled by the nurses’ arms in precious cradles made of gold. But now, in the middle of a forest and in a worn-out shed of thatch, the poor woman suffers neglected by her husband as a great

recluse.

In aflower garden where abounded jasmine creepers of full blown buds, that tender girl, lovely to behold and clad in white was merry, in the white moon. But now, in a region of thorns, filled with bamboos, the young woman suffers, clad in bark, with faded lustre and limping gait. In an excellent pond of crystal water, and in the midst of lotus blossoms, she was a beautiful fish leaping and sporting away as a creeper of lightning, swimming up and about. But now she lies shrivelled up dry and parched up by thirst : she, the virtuous and

(‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø, ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§)

‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡•§

‡§ï‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•Ä ‚Äî‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç‡•§

beautiful remains plunged in grief owing to her husband’s separation.

He bound with chains the Kinnara nymph, that was soaring at large in the heavens, a lovely parrot devoted to music, and confined the pitiable creature trembling all over the body in a cage.

Now, the she-parrot cries out in despair and agony with her beak thrust under the wings; the poor creature implores the giver of all boons, the best beloved of all that is dear, for emancipation.

(Pacing forward and looking about,) servant, how is her majesty engaged ? Is it a suitable hour for visit ?

Chamberlain.‚Äï I shall communicate if you command.
Sumati.‚Äî Madam, how does her majesty spend time ?

‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§¨‡•Ä‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§ï‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∏‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ï‡§≤‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ú‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•• ‡•Æ‡•® ‡••

‡§®‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ó‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§∂‡§π‡§§‡§≤‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä
‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§ï‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§õ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á ‡§µ‡•à‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§™‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡••

Chamberlain.‚ÄîThat charming lady devotedly attached to Lakshmi’s Lord, spends the day in divine worship and service. Her eyes closed and thoughts centred on her husband’s feet, she is looking forward to the path of emancipation. Considering that a heinous sin of her own rooted in some relentless Karma of old brought about a husband’s separation, she blesses her co-wife that she may obtain in abundance every kind of fortune derivable from meritorious acts.

The lotus eyed lady of slender limbs, is devoid of blood in both the cheeks, and resembles a creeper stricken by a thunderbolt. Constancy of devotion to her husband is her only ornament ; she the fairest and sweet has her lustre concealed by a garment of

‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•Ä‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç‡•§

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§)

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§Ü‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡•Ä ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§É‡•§

bark. Reposing all responsibility in the Lord that dwells in Vaikunta and protects the universe, she spends the time without desires, her thoughts centredon her husband, in the midst of good actions and discourses.
Sumati.‚Äî Communicate my arrival.

(Exit chamberlain).

Enter Suneeti.

Suneeti.‚Äî Brother, I bow.
Sumati.‚Äî May you get plenty of fortune; may you be blessed with the jewel of a son.
Suneeti.‚Äî The fruition of these benedictions may occur in another birth. Is my royal husband doing well; likewise sister Suruchi ?
Sumati.‚Äî They are doing well.
Suneeti.‚Äï Does my lord remember me occasionally ?

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî

‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ò‡•á‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¢‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•• ‡•Æ‡•™ ‡••

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî

‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•å‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡§®‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§æ ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§É
‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§µ‡§£‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ò‡§∏‡§®‡§Ç‡•§
‡§§‡§∞‡•Ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§™‡§ü‡§É ‡§ï‡•å‡§∂‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡§Ç
‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ ‡§¶‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•• ‡•Æ‡•´ ‡••

‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§π‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§Ø‡•ã-‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•á‡§£‡•§

Sumati.‚Äî I have no mind to mislead you by untruth O, auspicious and righteous woman ! The
monarch sleeps in dense darkness and never dreams of you.
Suneeti.‚ÄîTo me a cottage would be a mansion, the beasts of the jungle would serve as crowding relations, the gruel of the grains even without salt would be a highly relished dish and the tree-bark would serve as a clothing of great value‚Äîa dress of silk, if only there was the husband’s kind remembrance of me from a sense of my poor condition.
Sumati.‚Äî Everything is governed by Hari’s will. Let the time of redemption (grace) be awaited. Sister, I have brought some presents for your use; accept (them) with pleasure.

‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡§Ç
‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ï‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠ ‡§ï‡•á‡§§‡§ï‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§Ç‡•§
‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç
‡§®‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç‡•• ‡•Æ‡•¨ ‡••

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî

‡§ï‡•Å‡§Ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ã‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•á
‡§µ‡•á‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§ï‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡•§
‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç‡§¨‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ü‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ó‡•á
‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç‡••

Take (these) white kunda flowers of dazzling beauty forming a crown for the head. Here is the Kethaka (aloe) flower shining like burnished (pure) gold. Here is the plantain fruit brought from the hills of which you are greatly fond : here is a cake cooked sweet by (our) mother as your favourite dish.
Suneeti.‚Äï The Kunda flowers are beautiful when they are abundantly shared with a beloved husband in the Zest of love ; The braided hair is of enchanting beauty if there be a Lord to pull it (in sport). The plantain turns out the bitterest margosa, when the object of love is far away.
The mother-in-law is gratified only when a tasteful dish is served to her son-in-law, is it not ?

‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••
‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••
‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Å‡§Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ ‡§§‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••
‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§á‡§π ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§®‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡••

‡§π‡§§‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§ñ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ç‡§¨‡§∞ ‡§á‡§µ
‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§∏‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡•§

Sumati.‚Äî Queen, this is not to be rejected filled as it is with a mother’s ambrosial blessings, and filled also with Narayana’s grace, being an offering made to him.
Suneeti.‚Äî I am to eat only what remains of the food partaken by the husband ; nothing else, is it not ?
Sumati.‚Äî Eat this after offering it spiritually to Him who dwells within the husband : The result will be nothing but joy to you.
Suneeti.‚Äî Why will not my royal husband come here in person to eat it ?

I am condemned unheard like a deer shot unseen by the hunter’s arrows. I know not of any fault committed by me in my husband’s house that led to his getting offended. Vain becomes this birth (of mine) if I be marched to old age a barren woman at

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É** ‚Äî‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§ú‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§

whose hand no orthodox persons will accept water.
Sumati.‚Äî Queen, don’t be sorry. I will bring your lord here without delay, on some pretext or other.
Suneeti.‚Äî Just as the grateful savitri that rescued her husband from the jaws of death, adored Yama, so do I bow before Sumati out of gratitude, if you, O Sumati, show me out of supreme kindness one who is of untarnished lustre, who is ever fixed in my heart, who is honoured by Devas and who is my sovereign, my Lord, and my beloved.
Sumati.‚Äî Everything will turnout satisfactory. Don’t give way to grief.

ACT II. Scene IV.

Palace. Enter Suneeti, Manthara and Ganga.

Manthara.‚Äî By the favour of fortune, may your daughter beget an eminent warrior of nobility,
one whose greatness shall be famous in all directions, who shall he heard of even by Devas. Madam, your daughter will soon become the mother of a warrior son.
Ganga.‚Äî She is very weak : besides, this is her first delivery. I am greatly concerned about it
as to how a safe delivery will happen (how the tro lires will part).
Manthara.‚Äî The son that will be born will be of extraordinary lustre, being the result of a divine-gifted fruit.

‡§ó‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ ‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§É‡••
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‚Äî ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§Ü‡§É ! ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç, ‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§¶‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡••
‡§ó‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ ‚Äî‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡§ø‡§• ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§≠‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‚Äî‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§

‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç
‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Ç‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§•‡•ã ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á
‡§Ü‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ú‡§†‡§∞‡•á ‡§® ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§æ
‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§ñ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•ã‡§π‡§¶‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Å‡§Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç‡••

Ganga.‚Äî Everybody blesses him to be of unparalleled greatness.
Manthara.‚Äî It is rumoured that Suneeti also is pregnant.
Suruchi‚Äî Ah! what is it? Who is it that invented this false news?
Ganga.‚Äî Daughter, you said, is it not, that only one fruit was obtained by the king by the fulfilment of austerities. How is this news probable?
Suruchi.‚Äî I don’t believe the rumour.
Manthara.‚Äî I saw it with my own eyes. Her face is highly fair and shines beautifully with unusual light. The nipple is

black and the slender feminine hip looks big. Food is not retained in the stomach and she vomits often ; with the peculiar taste of pregnancy, she eats clods of earth with avidity. Where is the doubt in the matter ?
Suruchi.‚Äî Mother, I no longer wish to live nor to enjoy sovereignty after now hearing of the senior wife’s equal fortune as described : instead of beholding the prosperity of an enemy I am willing to suffer barrenness myself ; never can I bear equality with one who occupies the same position as myself, nor endure happiness in the lot of Suneeti.

(Hearing a deep sob.)

Ganga.‚Äî There are two questions to be asked in this matter.

Second. It is an assertion of the astrologers that without a boon, a son is not to be born to his majesty. If then the fruit brought was only one, what becomes of the prediction (of astrologers).

Suruchi.‚Äî (Looking at Manthara.) Let the two questions be answered.

or crook, by fair means or deception, her husband should be brought to her without delay. She said in fact:‚Äî

“My Lord has not come, and my condition is one unfit to be disclosed; people will speak of me as loose in conduct owing to loss of virtue. Intelligent Sumati, I shall feel grateful to you for a hundred births if you bring him to me for silencing the tongue of scandal.

Ganga.‚ÄîThis is news pregnant with meaning, and is enough to accomplish Suneeti’s ruin. Daughter, strenuous effort should be made so that the king may not hereafter even think of that direction.

Ganga.‚Äî Daughter, why are you impatient. Let the servant return. (Servant by a toss of the curtain.)
Servant.‚Äî They say that he left only yesterday for the forest to hunt and that he has not returned yet.

Manthara.‚Äî Undoubtedly, this is Sumati’s work.
Ganga.‚Äî We will think of another course.

Exeunt.

ACT III.
SCENE I.
A hermitage in the forest.
Enter Suneeti & Manthara.

Manthara.‚Äî Suruchi rejoices very much, having heard of your son’s beauty and excellent qualities.
Suneeti.‚Äî Does Suruchi remember me, unfortunate as I am?
Manthara.‚Äî Indeed, Suruchi remembers you with tearful eyes of sympathy, afflicted to see the hard-hearted monarch (so) perverse. Some-

‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§¶‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡•§

times she even utters harsh language and praises you and your boy in the presence of the king.
Suneeti.‚Äî I am obliged to her.
Manthara.‚Äî But without any reason, your memory is unpleasant to the king.
Suneeti.‚Äî This is a decree of fate. Is the sister’s boy growing up well?
Manthara.‚Äî Suruchi is unfortunate in that respect you are to be pitied for a husband’s absence and she, on account of a son who is but a living corpse.

In the world, God gives to man a fine intellect only in exchange for the calamity of congenital blindness. To you, he has given a son with talents like those of the immortals

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‚Äî‡§Ö‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‚Äî‡§á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡•§

‡§ï‡§¶‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç‡•§
‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É‡•• ‡•Ø‡•≠ ‡••

and to her, He has given a son whose body is a bag of boneless flesh.
Suneeti.‚Äî I am pained to hear this. I thought that Suruchi was fortunate in every respect.
Manthara.‚Äî Rare indeed is such partiality on the part of the Creator.
Suneeti. ‚ÄîEven so, I do not perceive an equality between us.
Manthara.‚Äî This indeed is the way of the world everywhere. To all men, what is not possessed by them or what is impossible to obtain is just what seems covetable. Suruchi deems the absence of a husband preferable to the misfortune of a worthless son. Possessed of a fine jewel of a son, you consider (however) the love of a husband preferable.

‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§ó‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•É‡§Ç‡§≠‡§§‡•á
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§£‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡•• ‡•Ø‡•Æ ‡••

(‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä)

‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§ø, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç‡••

Queen, I wish to see Dhruva; where is the boy?
Suneeti.‚Äî (Looking at the servant). Let the boy be brought.

Enter Dhruva and the nurse.

Nurse.‚Äî Blessed are you, O madam! see your excellent son of admirable intelligence. He wants ‘uncle moon’to be brought to him as a toy to play with. Casting away the toys in anger, he longs to soar up into the sky. He says that his place is in the heavens and that he will play with the stars.

(Suneeti fondles the boy).

Suneeti.‚Äî Friend, why is his body covered with dust

‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ñ‡§≤‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡§¶‡§ú‡§Ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ã‡§®‡•Å‡§¨‡§π‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•á
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡•• ‡•ß‡•¶‡•¶ ‡••

Nurse.‚Äî Madam, I took the boy when he was crying to the bank of the lotus pond; there the white swan was sporting in clear water without any concern. It danced on the lotus, with musical peals of sound and kissed the lotus leaf. Listening with attention, he heard the swan’s voice echoed in the caves of the forest and asked to my surprise who was making the sound of reply. Unable to answer, I said that there resided in the cave a strange boy Krishna by name. He then starts at once to go and play with him. He sets out pacing slowly into the forest with fearlessaudacity; when pursued, he runs laughing and trips when turning round to look behind

him like a lion. When told that numerous beasts of prey resided in the woods, he gently lisps saying “I have really the strength to fight with the animals of the jungle”. Wonderful, such courage for a boy of three years old!! When he tripped a little, his body became smeared with dust.

Manthara.‚Äî Queen, does the boy speak?
Suneeti.‚Äî Darling, speak out; where had you been?
Boy.‚Äî To play with the boy dwelling in the cave.
Suneeti.‚Äî (to herself.)

Young Krishna, an ocean of grace divine, O Hari, protect my son constantly; do protect with tenderness, my son Dhruva a child that has no protector, forsaken by his own father one ‚Äî that though born with

poor luck, represents to me the valued reward of good deeds done in by-gone janmas (incarnations), an only fruit as of a plantain tree, and rare as a paddy sprout grown on a piece of rock.
Manthara.‚Äî (taking the boy) Darling, come; I willgive flowers and fruits to you. Here are toys; your majesty, see the things sent by Suruchi. Fruits viz. wood apples, ebony rose apples, Amalakas<MISSING_FIG href=”../books_images/U-IMG-1721189312Screenshot2024-07-17093805.png”/>(Emblic myrobalan) Pomegranate, Mangoes and plantains; similarly, this painted peacock for the boy; this image of Vencatasa.
Boy.‚Äî (Taking theme) whence were these brought?
Manthara.‚Äî From your father’s house.

   ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§¨ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•á ‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏, ‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ç‡•§
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡§É ? ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§Ç‡•§

Boy.‚ÄîMamma, who is the father that sends me beautiful things like these?
Manthara.‚Äî Your father is an honoured monarch in possession of enormous wealth.
**Boy.‚Äî**Let mamma speak, not you. Mother, have I got a father? If so, who is it?

(Seeing tear drops in her eyes.)
Mamma, why are your eyes suffused with tears?

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Darling, the recollection of your father produced a slight flow of tears.
**Boy.‚Äî**Is father a cruel person? does he rebuke you, now that a mere recollection of him produces tears in you.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§•‡§æ ‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡§É‡•§ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§É‡••

‡§§‡§µ ‡§ú‡§®‡§ï‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ ‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡§ø‡§Ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç
‡§µ‡§∞‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•Å‡§≤‡§π‡§∏‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç‡•§
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§â‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§Ç‡••

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Not so at all is my lord. Your father indeed is very amiable.
Alas! your father’s countenance is a refreshing disc of the moon. That pair of excellent eyes shining like lotus is lovely. His soft and smiling utterance, is a soothing attar of roses. His intellect, dignity and qualities produce an ecstasy of feeling, the hair standing on end.

**Boy.‚Äî**I wish to go for seeing him.
**Suneeti.‚Äî**Let it be in proper time.
**Manthara.‚Äî**The boy may be affected by evil eyes. Taking the boy inside the house, let your majesty perform the rite for averting the evil influence of wicked eyes. I go to Suruchi’s quarters.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§

(‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ)

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§õ‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî ‡§è‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§µ‡§®‡§ó‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§

** ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä**‚Äî ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ø, ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡••

** ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä** ‚Äî

‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡•Ä‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ó‡•Å‡§°‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§ü‡•á ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§

Suneeti.‚Äî Communicate my constant remembrance to her.

Manthara.‚Äî As your majesty commands. (Exit Manthara).

Suneeti.‚Äî Boy, eat any one of these edibles, if you wish.

Boy.‚Äî I don’t wish to eat alone. I will eat in company with Krishna of the forest. Nurse. Let some other fruit that is at home be given, not one of these. It may be that strong affection raises mistrust; anyhow my mind suspects.

Suneeti.‚Äî Madam, what is the cause of suspicion?

Nurse.‚Äî Even the ants don’t rush at the sweet sugar, though they go about close by. They are in-

‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡•©‡••

(‡§®‡•á‡§™‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á) ‡§π‡§æ ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡§π‡§æ ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡•§

(‡§™‡§ü‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É)

** ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî‡§Ö‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç! ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É! ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡•Ä! ‡§π‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ! ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç?

** ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî

‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á
‡§õ‡§ó‡§≤‡§ï‡§ó‡§£‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§∂‡§®‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§π‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§¶‡§®‡§ï‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ñ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡§Ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡•©‡••

deed strange edibles, from which even flies remain scared away.

(Behind scenes) Alas! Alas!

(Enter servant with a toss of curtain).

Servant.‚Äî A disaster has happened; where is the boy! Is he safe? Alas that woman! how shall I relate it?

Suneeti.‚ÄîWhat, sirrah, is this wild utterance?

Servant.‚Äî Manthara being a stranger-woman, (unseen before) the watch-dogs of the sheep-pen seeing her on the road, barked at her; she fled with speed afraid of being bitten; and they did bite off a piece of flesh with sharp-edged teeth.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§Ü‡§É! ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï, ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§ó‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§ü‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ñ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§µ‡§¶ ‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡•á‡§®‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî

‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§Ç‡§ö‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä**‚Äî ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ø‡•§ ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Ü‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡•§ ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•§

Suneeti.‚Äî Ah! sirrah, peon. what is this?
If a visitor of my house, be bitten by dogs, the censure falls only on me. I don’t know if my innocent and faithful toilette-servant is alive or not. It is you that have by carelessness killed my friend.

Servant.‚Äî There is still something to hear. Let your majesty listen.

Suneeti.‚ÄîSay it quickly.

Servant.‚Äî Then it happened, that the woman dropped this cake on the floor. By devouring it, all the dogs quickly met with death.

Nurse.‚Äî Queen, my suspicion has been confirmed. This verily is the same as the one given to the boy.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ó‡•ã‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡•§

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§¨‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§® ‡§≠‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡•§ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•§ ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§

‡•• ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡••

‡•• ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É ‡•®‡••

(‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•§)

Suneeti.‚Äî A serious danger has been averted from my darling child, by the grace of Lord Krishna who is a kinsman of all afflicted people and a sea of kindliness. I did not know that Manthara was a tigress with the face of a cow. Servant, let all the flowers, fruits and toys be thrown away quickly, every one of them.

Boy.‚Äî Mamma, why are these removed from here?

Suneeti.‚ÄïThey are saturated with poison, and unfit to be eaten and unfit also to be offered to the boy Krishna.

(Exeunt)

SCENE II.

In the palace, Enter King, Suruchi and servant.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî** ‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡•§
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•å ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•å‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî ‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§¶‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•Ä‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•à‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ?
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§

King.‚Äî Then, what next?

Suruchi.‚Äî Being dog-bitten, she became bedridden for two years.

King.‚Äî It is perceived beyond doubt that Suneeti is wicked: a woman that causes her innocent and helpless toilette-servant, to be bitten by dogs, taking undue advantage of an opportunity, must be a very hard-hearted person indeed. How is it that it was not heard of by me for two years.

Suruchi.‚Äî I did not mention this to my royal husband out of regard for the position of the senior queen, and being afraid of tale-telling.

King.‚Äî This causes uneasiness; why did she go there?

Suruchi.‚ÄîI do not know, she should herself be questioned,

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§ö‡•á‡§ü‡•Ä? ‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§π ‡§ö‡•á‡§ü‡•Ä‡•§

‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É‡••

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§ü‡•Ä ‡§ñ‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä)

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ** ‚Äî (‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ)

‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã ‡§∏‡§ï‡§≤‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã
‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§¶‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§ï‡•Ä‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡•á
‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§Ç‡§•‡§ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ** ‚Äî ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§™‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡•§

King‚Äî Where is the toilette-servant? Sirral, let the toilette-servant come here.

(Exit servant)

Enter toilette-servant limping.

Manthara.‚Äî(Prostrating at the king’s feet.) O, monarch of justice, kinsman of the poor and the afflicted, see, sir, the wounded foot diseased with vermin in consequence of bites. O, king. I sacrifice this body at your feet; and the enemies of mine, - let them live in exultation.

King.‚Äî This may be accidental.

Manthara.‚Äî As God is my witness, I swear that the dogs were set on by Suneeti.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç‡§§‡§®‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§™‡§ü‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞?

** ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ö‡•Ç‡§°‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø‡§Ç‡••‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî‡§Ü‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡••

(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§ü‡•Ä)

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É**‚Äî ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã, ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡§™‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§É‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É**‚Äî‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É

[ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É]

King.‚Äî Good Madan, don’t fear. I will not forget your long and faithful service. I will order compensation (Pension) for your sufferings in our service; for what purpose did you go there?

Manthara.‚Äî To see my mistress the queen; so also to see her matchless boy, out of mere affection.

King.‚Äî I will consider your case; you may retire.

Doorkeeper.‚Äî My lord, some dwellers of the forest, accompanied by a nurse have come and (they) pray for an audience of your majesty.

**King.‚Äî**Cause them to enter.

Doorkeeper.‚ÄîAs your majesty commmands.

(‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É)

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî** (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç)

‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•à‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∞‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§É
‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡•Ä‡§≤‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§≤‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å ‡§∞‡§¶‡§õ‡§¶‡•á ‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§É
‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä**‚Äî (‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø)‡•§

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç?

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§≠‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç‡•§

(Enter Dhruva, Nurse and others.)

King.‚Äî (To himself) Is it a lion that approaches (me) ora splendid boy of extraordinarily majestic looks? This shining form, is it a human body ora creation from the leaves of blue-lotus. The sweet smile on the lips and in the eyes vanquishes the world by its emotion. Who is he that purloins my heart by a divinely enchanting figure of cupid?

Nurse.‚Äî (Whispers in the boy’s ear.)

Boy.‚Äî Father, I prostrate.

Suruchi.‚Äî Who you?

Boy.‚Äî I amthe son of the king on the throne.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É?
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•§
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§≤‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç‡•§
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äî** ‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§ (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø)
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É** ‚Äì ‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤, ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§µ‡•§ (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø)
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É** ‚Äî ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ?
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‚Äî‡§§‡§µ ‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•§
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É** ‚Äî(‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ) ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É?
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É** ‚Äî ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§¶‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ï‡§≤‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äì ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç, ‡§® ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡§µ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ?
** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡•§

**Suruchi‚Äî**Are you the son of Suneeti?
Boy.‚Äî Also Suneeti’s son.
Suruchi.‚Äî Boy, what is your wish?
Boy.‚Äî Nothing, I go to the lap of my father (So he goes.)
Suruchi.‚Äî Sirrah, boy, stand back there as you are (she stops the boy)
Boy. ‚Äî What is the cause of this obstruction?
**Suruchi.‚Äî**Only your misfortune.
Boy.‚Äî (With tremor of coice) why am I unfortunate?
Suruchi.‚Äî Because you were born of my co-wife in stead of from my womb.
Boy.‚Äî O king, is not my mother your lawful wife?
King.‚Äî Yes, what of it?

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É‚Äî** ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É\‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É** ‚Äî‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡•• ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§É‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç) ‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É** ‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Ç ?

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ?

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡•Ä ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§¨‡§æ
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§°‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•Ä ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§® ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ
‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡••

Boy.‚Äî Then, I am your son and fit to ascend the throne.

Suruchi.‚Äî Boy, you were not born out of Narayana’s grace; worship the Lord, then you will be competent and not otherwise.

King.‚Äî (to himself) Indeed a single fruit was brought and eaten away by Suruchi.

Boy.‚ÄîDoes not my mother worship Narayana ?

King. ‚Äî How do I know ?

Boy. ‚Äî Her majesty, the anointed queen, my chaste mother, of virtues honoured by the Gods is a devout worshipper of Hari. There exits not on the face of the Earth another virtuous woman equal or superior to her.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§∞‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§∂, ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî (‡§®‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É) ‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ?

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç)

‡§ù‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç
‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡•§
‡§ú‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç
‡§µ‡§∞‡§´‡§≤‡§ú‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É‡••

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç)

‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‡•§ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç‡••

**Suruchi.‚Äî**Sirrah, youngster, my royal husband knows the character of your mother.

Boy.‚Äî (With tears in his eyes) father, is the step-mother’s language approved by you?

King.‚Äî (To himself) The sudden outburst of words ringing deep like a bell and the eyebrows knit together in vindication of a mother, creates in me an unbounded trust in, and affection for, him. This boy of mine must be the one born out of the boon‚Äîgifted fruit. (aloud) Boy, let the discussion alone; go to your mother,

** ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É**‚Äî‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§®‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É

‡•• ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡••

‡••‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É ‡•ß‡••

(‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•á ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É)

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É**‚Äî

‡§ó‡§æ‡§¢‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§™‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§ó‡•ã‡§ö‡§∞‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§™‡§•‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§ø‡§Ç‡§π‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§™‡§ø‡§∂‡•É‡§ó‡§æ‡§≤‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§¶‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡•ã

**Boy.‚Äî**Not to my mother; but to Krishna dwelling in the forest, the refuge of the afflicted do I go. (Exit Dhruva running away) Exeunt all.)

ACT III. SCENE 3.

In the forest. Dhrura

Dhruva.‚ÄîDense is the forest; even at midday it is so dark here. The paths are wretched tracks filled with thorns not discernible by the eye. The frightful yell of beasts such as the tiger and the jackals fills the space in all directions. I do not know within what cave that Hari remains concealed.

(Calls aloud saying O! Nara Hari)
(Behind the scenes hearing Veena music)

O joy, the music of a great sage is heard!

Enter Narada.

Boy.~~ ~~ The wordy arrows of a stepmother having pierced through my sides, I am running away, O ! sage, into the jungle like a deer writhing from a (hunter’s) dart.

Boy~~ ~~. The time is past, when my wish was fixed on a low object. I prostrate before you. O, Sea of kindly grace, save me by instruction in divine truths.

(Falls at the feet).

Narada.‚Äî Boy, get up ; I will initiate you.

Boy.‚Äî I am saved.

**Narada.~~ ~~**Sit down; may Lord Narayana shower blessings on you, (secretly instructs him in the Manthra ‚ÄúOm Namo Vasudevaya".

(Then aloud.)

O prince, the body is not you but Dhruva is within. Jeeva (soul) is indeed an eternal self chained in this diminutive body of yours. Truly Narayana is the Lord shining as the original form of which everything else is a reflection.He alone is self-existent, the ruler of all the universe.

This is not an only body. There are several sheaths encasing you.From this bondage of sheaths, your emancipation will occur by the grace of Hari.

If you be one inherently fit to attain Heaven,

you will see Hari in person by His grace. The study of Narayana is the only means of obtaining His vision.

Your bliss is preordained and limited. You will get it in Moksha in the proximity of Hari. From Bramha to a particle of dust, the Jeevas are classed in gradation.

Persons who after realising the properties of things viz. whether they be transient, eternal and so forth, by the instrumentality of knowledge-sources such as perception, inference, and revelation, (1) become disattached to the objects of senses (2) acquire equanimity, control of mind and so on (3) look forward to liberation as the goal; (4) rely on Vasudeva

‡§°‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§π‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§§ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§É ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§™ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§≤‡§æ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ‡§ö‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§É‡•• ‡§ì‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡••‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡••

(‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‡••)

as the sole refuge (5) practice study, reflec- tion and concentration, for a long time with uninterrupted fervour in respect to Him (6) obtain a vision of the Lord (7) exhaust their karma in the plenitude of overflowing devotion, either by working it out or by the force of divine knowledge, with the help of His grace, (8) merge into higher forms or fly up from the mortal frame through the Bramha nerve (9) reach the Lord at Vaikunta along with Hiranyagarbha by routs suitable to them or by the paths of such as Archi (10) and freed altogether from unhappiness, enjoy in the vicinity of His personal presence and according to their rank, a bliss divine, by means of their spiritual essence or forms created for the time by mere volition ‚Äî‚Äî these do not incarnate again: such is the condensed essence of the sastras. Om Tat Sat.

(Narada retires.)

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**(‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç‡•§)

‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§®‡•É‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ü‡•ç‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á
‡§ñ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç‡••

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ
‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ú‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§á‡§π‡••

‡§Ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§
‡§§‡•à‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•à‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç
‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§≤‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç‡••

Dhruva.‚Äî(To himself)

I was born in this world O! Narahari, by the force of the king’s penance in order to work out my Karma. In the womb of Suneeti replete with worms & faces, I suffered every kind of pain.

O Madhava, I had no wish to form the acquaintance of a father and mother; bound with ropes by time and the sins of Karma I have been led hither.

A nurse and a mother strangled me by an abundance of ill-timed sleep and food. I suffered immeasurable pain, by swallowing doses of oil, with abundant weepings. (cries).

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•Ç‡§∑‡§£‡§™‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç
‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç‡••

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ï‡§£‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ß‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç‡••

‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ
‡§§‡§¶‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§ñ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ ‡§®‡•ã ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§π‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø-
‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§´‡§≤‡§ï‡•á ‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§∞‡•á‡••

**Dhruva.‚Äî**In birthafter birth, when I suckled the mother’s milk, what dropped on the floor in the suckling would make up an ocean of milk.

So incalculable have been the births I have undergone.

The drops of tears I have shed, will if collected together, make up a sea. O, Madhava in the course of births beyond all calculation I have undergone sufferings of every kind of description. (At last) deeming the monarch’s lap as heaven, I was distracted by the failure to attain it. O, Madhava let no desire be directed towards transient fruits that only rivet bondage.

‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç
‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡§®‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•à‡§∞‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§∏‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á
‡§¶‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•á ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡••

‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ß‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••

‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ
‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§ï‡§•‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

Liberate the boy given to play‚Äî who weeps or laughs without cause. Render my human incarnation fruitful of its purposes; forlorn do I beseech the lord.

To thee the lord Purusha, who being the reservoir of every force, by His greatness permeates and vivifies this utterance of mine so long dormant, and likewise permeates and vivifies the other organs such as the hands, legs, body, and the pranas, be this prostration.

The exquisite pleasure derivable by men from a meditation of Thy lotus feet and a study of the biography of Thy devotees, cannot be attained even in heaven, in the enjoyment of one’s own spiritual greatness.

‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§• ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç
‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§≤‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§)

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§É ‡••

Need it be said that it is unattainable by those who occupy positions from which they are ejected by the sword of death.

(Exit)

The end of Act III.

‡••‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É ‡•ß‡••

(‡§∏‡•å‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ö‡•§)

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É?

‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§¢‡§æ ‡§ï‡§≤‡§π‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§Ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•Ä
‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡••
‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•á‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã
‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ã ‡§¶‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡••

ACT IV. SCENE I.

In palace. (Enter Sumati and the king).

**King‚Äî**O Sumati, is there on Earth, or elsewhere, a man so unfortunate as myself?

The senior wife is a lover of quarrels, and is enjoying herself without any concern, her thoughts bent on pleasure. The other is so mean as to be ever prepared with girded loins to wage war with a child. This son of mine born of Suruchi is virtually a corpse, and deserves not the name ‘Uttama’: above all, (my son)**the genius has gone to the jungle. Who is there so miserable in misfortune as myself?

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É‡•§

‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡§æ
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§¶‡§π‡§®‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••
‡§® ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç
‡§ï‡§≤‡§π‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§Ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§∂‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**

‡§ï‡§•‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡§§‡•å ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§ï‡§¶‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•á
‡§µ‡§®‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••

**Sumati.‚Äî**I am liable to be suspected of partiality as the brother of Suneeti. However to speak the truth is my duty.

Ever devoted to Hari and trustful in the lead of a husband’s footstep, Suneeti is pining away emaciated by the fire of a lover’s longing. The word of tale-bearers should not be listened to with trust. The propensity for mischief attributed to her is as false as the horn of a hare.

**King.‚Äî**What say you, Sumati, in the matter of Man- thara? Is she a good-natured woman who thus instigates the biting by dogs. No, my wives are neither of them deserving of praise. An exile into the forest or suicide is the only course to be thought of by me.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡•á‡§Ø‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§Æ‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§•‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á, ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§∑‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç‡•§‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡••‡§Æ‡•á ‡§® ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§

‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ò‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ò‡§æ
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡••

**Sumati.‚Äî**This Manthara is wicked by nature and resembles the Manthara of Kaikeyi. My lord, her story is false. This is what people say.

**King.‚Äî**There is not the slightest proof that it is false. Let it alone: their topic is unpleasant to me. My head reels: the floor too whirls likewise. Friend I am almost mad. There is indeed no consolation for me.

**Sumati.‚Äî**Your excellent boy will surely return, with the aid of Narayana’s grace. Verily intelligence of that order must have originated only from the supreme grace of Vishnu.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**

‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§•‡•ã ‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§® ‡§≤‡•ã‡§π‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ü‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§≠‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£?‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§ö‡•Ç‡§§‡§´‡§≤‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§ø‡•§ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

**King.‚Äî**He who surpasses cupid forcibly steals my thoughts. No magnet possesses the attractive force of this boy. Without doubt Dhruva may be a product of divine grace. How can he be of such brightness otherwise.

**Sumati.‚Äî**Is this only a probability ? How is it forgotten by your majesty ? He is truly (a boy) born of the mango fruit obtained by the grace of Narayana.

**King.‚Äî**Not so; only a single fruit was brought and wholly eaten away by Suruchi. How then can Dhruva be the result of a boon?

**Sumati.‚Äî**My lord, he is really the result of a boon. I wonder how it is still unknown to your majesty. I pray your majesty will listen.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî (‡§Ü‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‡§π‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç
‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É‡•§

The proud queen Suruchi swallowed only the juice, casting away the seed. I gave that to Suneeti and hence Dhruva is a genius.
(full of brilliant qualities).

King.‚Äî (Thoughtfully) Friend, great is my gratitude for you. Fool that I was, I suspected Suneeti without inquiry. This news greatly increases my grief.

Gone is he my excellent boy into the dense jungle. What is the right course to be adopted by me? I will not live, no indeed, no indeed.

Sumati. ‚Äî Do not be broken hearted Omaster. I am

your slave attached to your footstep. If commanded, I will cause a search to be made all over the globe.

King. ‚Äî OSumati, bring hither the soul stirring son, whose face is fresh as lotus, whose voice rings majestic as the swan’s, whose eyes are broad and charming and who casts a spell on all that have common eyes to see.

In the whole world, where is the boy Ofriend, shining with an equal figure or where in the whole world is there a wretched king equal to me in being plunged in stupidity?

Sumati.‚Äî Every human endeavour shall be made to find Dhruva.

King.‚Äî Friend, see there the anklet of the child. (To himself)

The anklet which shone by contact with your charming ankle, alas! lies there, having forsaken the soft music natural to it. Darling boy, where do you wander now, after deserting and forgetting your best friend, a follower of your footsteps.
(Behind scenes) “This way, thisway your majesty”.

(Enter Suruchi hurriedly).

Exit Sumati.

Suruchi falls at feet.

King.‚Äî What is the crime you committed.

Suruchi.‚Äî I am a sinner.
