** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç) ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§•‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§ (‡§®‡•á‡§™‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•§)

‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ, ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ,

‘‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç’

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É)

was. Accidentally (or by God’s will) I happened to be bitten by dogs and was punished by Hari. I am giving up the ghost O! King; may Suneeti become the jewel of your head. If there be any good luck still left to you. you will get back the tiger of a boy.

King.‚Äî(to himself.) By this news my eyes are opened. I am accursed in every way.
(Behind scenes.) ‚ÄúHelp, help. We wish to see the king.‚Äù

Enter servant.

** ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§

(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§É ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É)
(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É)

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É**‚Äî ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É‡•§ ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§É ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É**‚Äî ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Ä‡§∞‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§ü‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ñ‡•á
‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§£‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§≤‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ó‡§æ ‡§ó‡§ó‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§π‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ
‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

Servant.‚Äî Your majesty, a few foresters beseech an audience.

**King.‚Äî**Cause them to enter.

Exit servant and Suruchi.

Enter subjects.

Subjects. ‚Äî May his majesty be victorious! Victorious! fearful indeed are the portents observed. We crave protection.

First man.‚Äî Your majesty, I am a forester; and near my cottage,

A fire suddenly sprang up from the ground. upward into the sky, a pillar-like collection of flames. The birds travelling in numbers fell from the sky to the Earth consumed by the unendurable heat.

** ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§®‡§µ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§≠‡§∞‡§æ ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•Ä
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡•ã‡§∞‡§ï‡§µ‡•É‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡•§
‡§ù‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§≠‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ ‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ
‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ó‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ ‡§π‡§§‡•á‡§µ‡••

** ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§≤‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡§Ç
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ü‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§≤‡§æ‡§§ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

[‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É]

Second man.‚ÄîThe Tamala creeper weighted with fresh blossoms charming to look at, with stalks of blossoming buds, lost lustre and withered dry all on a sudden, like one struck dead by a severe heart-disease.

Third man.‚Äî O overeign, the Earth vibrates quickly, the bowels of the Earth rumble like thunder. The houses tremble with fear owing to the Earthquake, and fear splits asunder the hearts of men.

King.‚Äî Subjects, you may take leave; we will inquire into this matter.

(Exeunt subjects)

[‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•á]

‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§°‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•Å‡§Ç
‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•å‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§ß‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§≤‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ
‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•• ‡•ß‡•´‡•≠‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•Ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡•§

‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∂‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§É‡•§

[‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á]

‡•• ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï ‡•®‡••

[ ‡§∏‡•å‡§ß‡•á‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•§ ]

A voice in the sky.

Having given up a son honoured by the Gods, good gracious! this Old man is gambolling with damsels. Shame does not smart him, although Dhruva reigns supreme as a yogi (Divine thinker).

King.‚Äî Who is this man that speaks impertinently of me. It seems forgotten that this Uttanapadais a warrior.

Peon, let the bow and arrows be got ready.

Exeunt.

ACT IV.SCENE II.

In the palace. Enter Suneeti and Suruchi.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ø ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§â‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§ó‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•´‡•Æ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§ó‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§Ç ‡§à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡§Ç‡••‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§∏‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡•§‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî

‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ó‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§

Suruchi.‚Äî O, Queen, welcome to you into the apartments of the palace; resume (your) position as the mistress of the household. His majesty has been very ill and bedridden from mental derangement.

Suneeti.‚Äî Alas! when my dearest darling went away into the forest, god alone knows the anguish of my unfortunate self. I roamed about, searching for my darling, day after day into the jungle without food. At this juncture, your letter was received containing news. What says his majesty !

Suruchi.‚Äî From mental disorder, he cries aloud for you as well as Dhruva that princely boy. After howling aloud, he desists only when

‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∞‡§¶‡§®‡§∞‡§£‡§ø‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ã
‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ã‡§¢‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ã ‡§® ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•´‡•Ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§Ü‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§≠‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§ø, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á‡§≤‡§ø‡§É‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§™‡•á ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡•§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡••

[‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É]

as an invalid, he becomes quite exhausted. At sight of me, he rattles his teeth, getting very ill from excitement. His majesty isunable to bear even the sound of my nameenter the hollow of his ears.

**Suneeti.‚Äï**The words of an invalid are prompted by his illness. Let it not be suspected that you are now not the favouriteof our royal husband.

Suruchi.~~** **~~If there be occasion, let not Suruchi be forgotten by your majesty.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Sister, is this a formality of speech or fun ?

**Suruchi.‚Äî**It is the command of the physician that Ishould not stay near the king. So I take leave.

Exit Suruchi.

(‡§™‡§ü‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡•á ‡§∂‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•§)

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** (‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ) (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç) ‡§π‡§Ç‡§§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡§É ‡§≤‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§§‡§™‡§≤‡§≤‡§É ‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∂‡•ã‡§≠‡§É ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ó‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É‡••

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî**(‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§Ç) ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ü‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§á‡§§‡§É‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§≤‡§≠ ‡§â‡§™‡§∂‡§Æ‡§É‡••

‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Ç
‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

(The screen lifted; on a bed, the king and the physician)
Suneeti.‚Äî (seeing) (to herself,) Alas, the change of the lord; one whose lustre shamed Indra’s glory,lies there, his fleshcompletely gone, his glow (of health) bedinnmed, his eyes and cheeks sunken deep into hollows. This formprevents me from even recognising him as my royal husband.

Physician. ‚Äî (Gently) Is it Queen Suneeti?

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Let the doctor command.

**Physician.‚Äî**Hereafter the cure is easy.See how, without delay, I dislodge the diseaseby the root. The phlegm superad-

‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ
‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡•¶‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•à‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç,‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§®‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§™‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§É‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§®‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§

‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç
‡§ö‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡•§

Suneeti‚ÄîYour skill is indeed renowned everywhere;but this seems to have taken time.

**Physician.‚Äî**There was not the slightest fault in me.Why did not your ladyship turn up earlier than this.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Sir,I said not by way of blaming.

**Physic‚Äî**See,the patient sleeps.This is an indication of progress towards convalescence.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**I rejoice to hear.

**Physician.‚Äî**See again,he laughs gently in sleep.With eyes closed,he feels a recognition of

** ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

Suneeti.‚ÄîMay his cure be accomplished quickly by your skill.

Physician.‚Äî(Feeling the hand.) The body is lukewarm. The pulse of the hand beats regulated as it should. He sleepsmotionless in bed,without any distortion of countenance. This disease was born in the brain from a rush ofblood into the head. Let everybody avoid all topics of sorrowful memory as well as reference to Dhruva~~ ~~Let the queen sit here at the edge of the bed and sing gently and slowly. That is the medicine hereafter.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî(‡§à‡§∑‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•á)‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•Å‡§ó‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•å ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•• (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É)‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî(‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø) ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡•§ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Exit Physician.

Suneeti.‚Äî(Doing so) (to herself) (thinking of Dhruwa) He shone with the melody of twinkling bells and the looks of a smiling laugh; my child soon wiped away the tears of all my suffering. I bore him for nine months and begot acupid equal to the Gods. The unbecoming ambition of ill-starred me was shattered by the will of God.

King.‚Äî (Slightly opening his eyes) wonderful! a soo thing, soft, majestic music, sweet as ambriosia to the ear. Who is itthat sings? (Wakes up in bed.)

Suneeti.‚Äî(Standing up,) your majesty, I prostrate. I am Suneeti, at your service, whose banishment has been cancelled.

King‚Äî My loyal wife? the mother of Dhruva?

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Does my royal lord remember me?

King~~~~Lovely woman, one shaft imbedded in my heart has now been extracted; forgive completely what was done atthe instigation of wicked tales. Let every trace of offence due to my heartless action vanish from your mind; O best beloved woman, Do not forsake me an invalid.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**Lord, being prompted by the will of Hari, my royal husband did it all. By nature kind to humanity, he certainly would not otherwisehave been unkind. This is my constant prayer to Srinivasa that my mind should always feelsatisfied in my lord.

Suneeti.~~ ~~ My lord, the topic of Dhruva is forbidden by the doctor.

King‚Äî Only one question. Does the child live?

Suneeti‚Äî He lives.

**King~~ ~~**How is it known to you that he lives?

Suneeti.‚Äî I will not reply; The physician’s word should be absolutely respected.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**He is gone into the forest in quest of the son

gambols with damsels". Hereafter, not with “damsels.” It should be read in the singular, the wicked Suruchi being virtually dead..
**Suneeti.~~ ~~**Your majesty, the malady grows by this excitement. Let your majesty sleep.

King.‚Äî ‚ÄúShame does not smart him.‚Äù Let it be read “But disease smarts him.”

Suneeti.‚Äî Peon, let the physician come quickly. (to herself) Is it not an utterance of delirium?

King. ‚Äî Sirrah, peon, stop there. Dear, I will desist. There is no need for the physician. I will talk of other matters. Dear, why did you delay your return?

Suneeti.‚Äî I did not know of your majesty’s illness.Only yesterday, came the news along with

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§≤‡•á‡§ñ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî ‡§á‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§ú‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî (‡§Ü‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•Ä‡§∏‡§æ ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ç
‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡•• ‡•ß‡•¨‡•≠‡••

the despatch cancelling my exile.

**King.‚Äî**It is three months since my signature was affixed.

**Suneeti.‚Äî**my lord, if permitted and if shown a kindness, I beg for a favour.

King.~~ ~~ Do not be afraid hereafter that misled by tales I shall again order your exile.

Suneeti.~~ ~~ I shall mention my prayer if approved in anticipation by the word ‚Äú granted‚Äù.

King.‚Äî (thinking) granted.

Suneeti.‚Äî Suruchi, the dear wife, is worthy of compassion. She a queen shall not be subjected to punishment.I knowthe sufferings of separation: Let bygones be bygones and all forgotten.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ**‚Äî (‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§É) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É‡•§‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡•Ä‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ** ‚Äî ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡••

‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§É‡••

King.~~~~(stunned by surprise) Dear, What is this? I am a fool to have given a promise. I will not see her face.

Suneeti.‚Äî The word of a Kshattriya has been given.She should be forgiven at once.

**King.‚Äî**Be it so.

(Exeunt)

End of Act.IV

SCENE 1.

In the forest. Enter M√°tali with Nandi.

**Matali:~~ ~~**Will the object of Lord Indra be attained? The residents of Swarya speak of the boy-sage as one possessing very great power.

Matali:‚Äî See, here is the burning flame in the north.The figure of the boy is also visible covered with dung-hill from which an unceasingcolumn of smoke is ascending.

** ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§≤‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

austerities or what is your object? Though you are but a boy, Oprince,the world trembles at your deeds of penance.

Dhruva:‚Äî Friend, the deity whom I love, and who is the object of worship to all pious men, resides in Vaikunta. Being greatly troubled in mind,and longing for final emancipation, I am eager to see Him. I prostratetion, myself at the lotus-feet of Sankara. For the attainment of my cherished goal, may Srikanta in his condescension bring about for me an interview with Vayu.

Matali:‚Äî If Vayu comes, will you desist from austerities?

Dhruva:‚Äï I will do so.

What is it you say?

With jewels of gold sounding sweet melody and the tinkling flute playing airs, with ballsports, dance, and amusements, in the midst of many tiny calves, do thou protect me. With the conchshells and wheels resplendent

on the shoulders, O thou wonderful cowherd, come to me. O Thou of faultless greatness, O Narayana, protector of the faithful, do come to me.

O rider of the bird, O King of smiling face, do Thou come with flashes of manifold ≈ìesthetics. I shall adore your greatness for ever here below ; OPurandara Vittala, do come to me.

(Then enter Krishna as a boy adorned as mentioned)

Vayu:‚ÄîOLord, adoration! adoration!
(Prostrates at feet.)

All prostrate, saying, Jaya, Jaya. Glory, glory.

Dhruva:‚ÄîThee from whom, the Vedas recoil. powerless to describe Thy (i. e. Vishnu’s) greatness, like a piece of cotton blown back by the impact of storm, Thee whom even the intellect of Lakshmi fails to grasp with a comprehension of all (Thy) attributes, how am I, a boy of lisping utterance, to praise, so great, as Thou art.

This poor individual, torn by the arrows of an enemy, approaches with awe, in quest of a ship, the great bliss-bodied Fish, that shone as a sun, destroyed the Asura, and was adored by the Solar king (Satyavrata). May the Fishgod swimming in the world-destroying waters of the deluge, protect me, a cripple whose thoughts are imprisoned in the meshes of the wicked fisherman Kali, in the flooding waves of birth.

Thy illusory tortoise-form was pleased to upheave Mandara, the mountain of Gold, when, being churned hard with an excess of sweating fatigue by the combined hosts of righteous Devas and jealous Daityas, and tossed by waves and winds, it was about to founder, like the mind of the wicked overpowered by the organs of sense. To that Tortoise bestowing bliss on the Devas, be this prostration of mine.

I bow here before this adored and universally adorable Boar-form God who feigned a slow and doubtful fight at first, and, being appealed to by the entreaty of Suras, killed the wicked and low son of Diti who was the arch-enemy of the most righteous of mankind and was elated by the pride of an immense prowess such as terrorised the vast hosts of Devas’ leaders.

Playful mind, address yourself to Him who is the destroyer of death itself, the adored deity of the Daitya boy, who assumed the form of an excellent lion-faced man to kill the garrulous Hiranya Kasipu, who rescued the hero of boys from dangerous situations in which he was sought to be killed by elephants, by fire, by the swallowing of a virulent poison, by drowning, and by a fall from the summit of a mountain, and who cured him of the fever of all accumulated sins.

To thee, the boy of liliputian guise, who saved Indra and humiliated Bali (the Daitya), and who destroyeth sins (of worshippers) as fire consumes a forest of down, be this prostration.

To thee, the Bramhan avatar (1) that was an ornament of the Bhrigu race, (2) that destroyed an unrighteous clan of kings (3),

Adore here that Hari (1) who is the father of Bramha (Sarasvati’s Lord), (2) who saved the Devas by boons, from the sufferings caused by Rakshasas the enemies of all sages, (3) who guarded the sacrifice of Visvamitra and of the Rishis with his fleet arrows, who snapped the bow of Siva the offspring of Bramha, a deity adored by Asuras of intense unbridled passions (4) who was the hero of the prayers (a) of the lady consigned to the forest by Mathanga’s curse and (b) of Sarabhanga the prince of ascetics and (c) of garuda (the God of birds).

I prostrate here before Damodara of a dark cloudy hue, the refuge of the suffering humanity, who, adorned in jewelry of gold, and clad in saphired robes, appeared and carried away the clothes of damsels,‚Äî who

treated emperors and leading Daityas as a lion does (a pack of) Jackals, ‚Äî who commanded in homage the bent heads of Devas,‚Äî who ruled the clan of cowherds shining with a face resplendent as that of the moon,‚Äî aand who is the sole faultless hero of all Vedic teachings.

O Buddha, who created delusion in the descendants of Diti by a system of Buddhistic philosophy that looked reasonable and consoling, do thou step in, and purify my mind by depriving it of impious Buddhistic theories. Vexed by the succession of births and deaths, I seek shelter of thee O Hari, known as Kalki, incarnated for the destruction of the wicked, riding on an excellent steed; forgive my sins, O Lord, and make me holy.

‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§§ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•å‡§®‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç‡•§
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§¶‡§ï‡•à‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ú‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡§Ç‡••‡•ß‡•Ø‡•¨‡••

a sage’s curse and from the onslaught of a foe, when, surrounded by herds of elephants the sworn enemies of the Areca and the honeyed sugarcane, in a lotus-pond filled with singing and intoxicated bees and situated in a beautiful pleasure-forest, he offered up a supplicating prayer, unable to endure the shock and agony caused by the attack and bite of the hidden prince of crocodiles.

O Vyasa, liberal fountain of boons, make me ardent in the pursuit of a wealth which consists in relishing the honeyed essence of Vedanta as elucidated by the shastras of Vayu.

Make me eminent with the lore esteemed by the sage Jaya the follower of the footsteps of Sri Madhwa the master of the Vedas. By means of the shastras codifying the vedic teachings and of holy water flowing from Hari’s feet, ordain me pure, standing as I do in supplication, with hands folded over the head.

‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç
‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç‡•§

‡§Ü‡§∞‡•Ç‡§¢‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§≤‡•á ‡§π‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É‡•§

On my head, place for ever the faultless ’lotus of foot’ that sanctifies its worshippers more than anything else deemed holy.

O Thou Lakshmi’s lord, source of the holiest stream, sovereign of all whose footstep is hallowed, May the lotus of foot now purify my mind. May this lotus of foot of inconceivable lustre, that metamorphosed a rock into a woman‚Äî which was pleased to roam about Brindavana, and which blessed cows and maids in the woods, be the fountain- head of a river consisting of my emancipation (salvation).

The same soft (lotus) flower of Vishnu which sat lightly on the shoulders of devoted Hanuman like a piece of cotton‚Äî the same

of Murari, which was impregnable as a thunder-bolt when it destroyed Sakata‚Äì and which rested like a nectar-pot on the palms of Garuda’s hand.

Let Thy foot which blessed Bali who bore it on his head, rest and dance upon my head. May that foot-lotus which subdued the unbounded arrogance of Kalinga, dislodge the spirit of Kali rankling in my heart.

I bow before that tender foot which glanced bright on the kunkuma in the bosoms of Vraja’s lovely maids when Thou wert an infant form, and which measured the three worlds in three paces in the subjugation of a Danava.

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡§≠‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¢‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç

‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ò‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§§‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§

May that foot-lotus save me, which, instead of being water-born (as its Sanskrit name imports) is glorious as the source of an abundant stream of sanctity, and which, instead of seeking sun’s rays for joy and luxuriance, perpetually imparts to the sun itself an abundance of heat and light.

May that all-protecting lotus of foot, be glorious, which expands myriads of petals at the prayer-ful music of devotees, which is always full-blown (never being a bud ) because of a perpetual vedic sun-shine ‚Äî which wafts a fragrance consisting of final felicity, ‚Äî which is filled with the honey of Grace, and which is adored by Padma (the lotus deity) herself. May that tender and beautiful pair of feet, a spirit dense of bliss ‚Äî that priceless and

magnificent blossom, unique lotus of the blood-red kind, pure and unfading, be the ornament of my head, whose contemplation alone renders devotees joyful and mad with the drinks of honey, so that withintellects dizzied by delirium they wander in the world renouncing all attachment to household concerns going by the name of wife and children, and looking in the eyes of men sometimes mute and sometimes deaf.

My lord, be Thou pleased out of affection to bathe this heated head of mine, consumed by the fires of Junma, with ambrosial showers of Thy pre-eminent grace, flowing from Thy ‘Foot lotus’ fragrant with cool and agreeable perfume.

** ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É**‚Äî (‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø)

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É**‚Äî (‡§Ü‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ)

‡§Ö‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á
‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•¶‡•Æ‡••

(Thus meditating swooned away.)

**Vayu.‚Äî**The Lord is about to bless you. He will grant your wish; get up quick.

Sri Krishna.‚Äî (raising by both hands) Boy, I am immensely pleased at your penances and prayers. Say quickly what is in your heart. I will soon grant your desire.

Dhruva.‚Äî (Thinking, and stunned as if mad, with tremor of voice) Indeed the cherished desire of my heart is suddenly forgotten, O Lord. It may be that I aimed at what I was unworthy to get. Save me ‚Äî one who seeksshelter.

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É‚Äî**

‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§∏‡•Å‡§Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ó ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞
‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•¶‡••

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•§ (‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á)

‡••‡§ï‡•Å‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§É ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡••
(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É)

Krishna.‚Äî Be this (your wish), the attainment of a position high as the moon and the stars. Be you monarch for a long time, the foremost in the galaxy of heavens.

Dhruva.‚Äî I am blessed by Thy favour.

**Krishna.‚Äî**Boy of slender limbs, cease from the pursuance of concentrated yoga. I am pleased to grant you, eminent prince, a constant faith in Achyuta.

**Dhruva.‚Äî**I deem the second boon very much greater than the first.

The Drum of Devas is heard.
Shower of flowers on Hari’s head.
Exeunt.

‡••‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§É‡••

‡••‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡••

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§∞‡•á ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ñ‡§≤‡§ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§§‡•á ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•§ ‡§á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§® ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ó‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••

Act V. Scene ii

In the forest. Enter Sumati and forester.

Sumati.‚Äî Well, forester, how far from here has it to be journeyed still ?

**Forester.‚Äî**The way appears somewhat missed.

Sumati.‚Äî Where is your smoke and flame; the sky ascending column of fire ‚Äî what was mentioned by you in the king’s presence.

**Forester‚Äî**I believe it was in this region. Now however it has disappeared.

Sumati.‚Äî What is to be done ?

Forester.‚Äî Turn back to the city.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**(‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ó‡§∞‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§≤ ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç, ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡•á ‡§µ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ã
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å
‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§ï‡§Ç‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•ß‡••

** **‡••‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡§É‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**

‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§®‡§§‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ß‡§É ‡§ñ‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§É
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§ø‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§∞‡§®‡•Ä‡§ß‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡§ü‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•§

**Sumati.‚Äî ** (Manifesting anger.) Have we wandered from forest to forest, all this time, day and night, only to return to the city without Dhruva. See, you deceitful fellow, I will cause you to enter the prison soon.

Forester‚Äî Sir, the column of fire seen by all, is now not to be found; nor do I see on the ground the crevice widened by earthquakes.

Goes forward and seeing,

By my luck, it is perceived that there is a hermitage close by, which has boys.

**Sumati.‚Äî**How is this gathered ?
Forester.‚Äî In this expansive Aswatha tree, low-ly-

‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç
‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•®‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§§‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§∞ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§â‡§ü‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡§ó‡•ã‡§ö‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É**‚Äî (‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ) ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§™‡§§‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§ü‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§õ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡•Ä‡§∞‡§É‡•§ ‡§á‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä, ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§õ‡§æ‡§µ‡§É‡••

‡•• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§Ç‡§¶‡•á‡••

**~~~~**ing twigs have been plucked by liliputian hands. Cloths seem to have been tied, (to the branches for drying) from the recently fallen drippings of water. The mark of water-drops on the ground indicates the cloths to have belonged to boys (fit only for them)

Moreover, sir, on the sand, the mark of diminutive foot-prints is in fact clearly visible.

Sumati.‚Äî This is true. Go in advance; and bring news if there be a cottage or hermitage within the range of sight.

Forester. ‚Äî(Doing so) Close at hand is a cottage of some Rishi hidden from view among the branches of trees. Here comes a tenant of the hermitage. Let us ask him.

Enters a hermit.

Sumati.‚Äî O Hermit, I salute.

** ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**‡§ì‡§Ç, ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§É‡••
** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡••
** ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É‚Äî

‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É
‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•Ä‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à ‡§®‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•©‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§∏‡§ö‡§ø‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã‡§É‡•§
‡§î‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§§‡•ç
‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•™‡••

** ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**

‡§á‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§É
‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§® ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§

Hermit.‚Äî Om: May your cherished wish be gratified.

**Sumati.‚Äî**If this benediction be fulfilled, then I am blessed.

**Hermit.‚Äî**Who are you sir, exhausted by journey, born of rank and dignified (by look)? Your journey does not appear prompted by dis- attachment to the world, nor for the sake of game.

Sumati.‚Äî I am the minister of the sovereign. I am searching for the master’s son. In great vexation, the son of king Uttanapada went to and lost his way in the forest.

**Hermit.‚Äî**There is a certain boy-sage here, who does not however seem to have lost his way‚Äî

‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã
‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§ß‡•Ä‡§É‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•´‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•¨‡••

** ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**

‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§Ç
‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•®‡•ß‡•≠‡••

(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡§É)

(‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§ö‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‡•§)

who is a master in blissful Renunciation, and who is a genius, with thoughts directed to the Heavenly path.

**Sumati.‚Äî**My boy is only five years old; How can he possess a knowledge of God, O sage? He is only fit to be initiated in the alphabet, and I search for him day and night.

**Hermit.‚Äî**The boy whom you are searching for, may or may not be the one I speak of; you better search; see there the boys gathering flowers.

Exit Hermit.

(Enter Soumya, Meenanka, Krishnadasa, plucking flowers).

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É** ‚Äî(‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç‡•§

‡§à‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ
‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•Ø‡•Æ‡••

(‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç) ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§™‡§Ç (‡§µ‡§ø‡§ü‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á ‡§â‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§É )

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É** ‚Äî‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§Ç, ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§ú‡•Ç‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§≤‡•à‡§É‡••

‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äì ‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∑‡•Å ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡§ø‡§°‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§≤‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§≤‡§≠‡§Ç‡•• ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§ü‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§É‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•ã‡§≤‡§É‡••

Sumati.‚Äî (to himself.)
O joy, rare indeed is the sight of juvenile ascetics like these, shining like incandescent coals and abounding in spiritual force.
(apart) Forester, stopping here, we will hear this talk. (They sit down among the trees)

**Krishnadasa‚Äî**Well, Soumya, hasten the collection of flowers. My basket is nearly full of Tulasi leaves.

**Soumya‚Äî**It is easier to gather Tulasi leaves than flowers, because Tulasi leaves remain crowding thick on the branches of the plant. Hence your basket is full and not ours of Kunda blossoms.

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É‚Äî**‡§® ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§≤‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§®‡•à‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É‚Äî‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ ‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§≤‡•Ä‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡•• ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§® ‡§Ø‡§§‡§§ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É**‚Äî‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§É‡••

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•å ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§É ‡§â‡§ü‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡••

**Meenanka‚Äî**I don’t think that is the reason. Our friend has a special skill in gleaning Tulasi leaves.

**Soumya‚Äî**What is this special skill?

**Meenanka‚Äî**Observe how he plucks them. It looks as if Tulasi, with a motherly love for devotees, rushes forward with effort into the regions of our friend’s fingers, rather than that he exerts himself to gather the leaves.

Soumya.‚Äî What is the cause of Tulasi’s enthusiasm?

Meenanka.‚Äî Affection for devotees.

Krishnadasa.‚Äî Friends, I go in advance to the cottage with your leave.

Soumya.‚Äî Your promise was to accompany us.

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** (‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç) ‡§∞‡•á ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡•§ ‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•Ä‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§É ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø ‡§®‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§ó‡§§‡•å ‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§® ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡•• ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡••

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É‚Äî**(‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø) ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** (‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç)‡•§‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§É‡••

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§§‡§™ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§¶‡•É‡§¢‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç‡§§‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∞‡§§‡§™‡§É

Sumati.‚Äî (apart) Well forester, who is the boy gathering Tulasi? There is something remarkable about his features, eyes, gait and speech.

Forester.‚Äî I do not know. As I saw from a great distance, I remember faintly that it was he that remained under the smoke of penance.

Meenanka. ‚Äî (to Krishnadasa) Why such hurry though your austerities have been finished ?

Forester.‚Äî (apart) Sir, please listen.

Krishnadasa.‚Äî If finished, why am I walking on the Earth?

Soumya.‚Äî A reference to penance reminds me ‚Äîhow strong-minded our friend was who went through the severest austerities for a long time without food and drink!

** ‡§µ‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** (‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∏‡•ã ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§®‡•Ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§µ‡§É‡••

‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§∏‡§®‡•á‡§õ‡§æ‡§µ‡•à‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî**

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç
‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§¶‡§¶‡•å ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§∂‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§¶‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ
‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§Ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ‡•• ‡•®‡•ß‡•Ø‡••

Forester.‚Äî (apart) Sir, this undoubtedly appears the sage.

Sumati.‚Äî Indeed, this creates hope.

Meenanka.‚Äî Even now he does not eat.

Soumya.‚Äî We will ask our friend himself. Friend, it is said that you eat nothing at all in the day or night. How came about this total absence of appetite (for eating) ?

Krishnadasa.‚Äî For a long time, the desire to eat and drink was unconquerable. It gave me constant and severe pain to control. Its pride and power abated after the vision of Vishnu, and the appetite vanished at the taste of the honeyed juice in the feet of Hari. (at the enjoyment of pleasures afforded by a contemplation of Hari).

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡§É‚Äî**‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ú‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡••

** ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‚Äî** (‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§∏‡§≠‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§É ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§à‡§∑‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç) ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡§Ç‡•§

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç‡••

Meenanka‚Äî We are still engaged in studying words and sentences in PramanaLakshana by repeated recitations, being dazzled by mere verbiage. We do not realize god even in imagination. But he has seen Lakshmi’s Lord in person and adored His Lotus feet.

Soumya‚Äî In other births have the Shastras been studied by him.

Meenanka‚Äî (Continuing to gather flowers) Soumya, observe this royal sage how he often sheds drops of tears. He is afflicted a little by grief. What may be the cause ?

Sumati.‚Äî (To himself) The word ‘Royal sage’ is a second ground of hope.
Soumya.‚Äî It is rumoured that his father is suffer-

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É**‚Äî‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É**‚Äî(‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Ç) ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡••

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É**‚Äî(‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø) ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É** ‚Äî

ing from a deranged mind. This news may be the cause.
Krishnadasa.‚Äî It is not now that my father is deranged in mind. His madness was quite evident when he married two wives.
Sumati.‚Äî (To himself) From this it is established that this is the boy. I will listen to the cause of grief. He may be anxious to return home.
Soumya.‚Äî (To Krishnadas) Then what is the cause of your uneasiness ?
Krishnadasa.‚Äî Before I was born, my father saw Vishnu the giver of Heaven (Moksha) ; and he contented himself with praying for a son, just as I under similar circumstances got the position of Dhruva. My family appears suffering under a curse, by reason of which, neither by me nor by my father Uttana pada, was Heaven (Moksha) secured, not. withstanding a personal vision of Lakshmi’s

‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ó‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§ï‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç‡•§‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** (‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø)

‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ó
‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ó‡§Ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§ö‡§≤‡§ó‡§§‡§ï‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç

(‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø)

** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî** (‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç) ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø, ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø-

Lord. This grief incessantly troubles me. We have gathered enough of flowers. Let us go.

Sumati.‚Äî (appears in a hurry) A moment here, will you stop, O, beautiful boy; my head whirls with the intoxication of excessive
joy; wiping aside my tears when the hands get steady, O Dhruva, I shall hug you, my sister’s son, to my bosom.(The boys look with surprise)

Krishnadasa.‚Äî (apart) Soumya, I understand that this is Sumati my maternal uncle. Hold the

** ‡§∏‡•å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏, ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§•‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•å‡••

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å, ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•å‡••

Tulasi basket for a moment, while I render him obeisance: (aloud) uncle, I prostrate.

Sumati.‚Äî Be you long-lived. (so embraces).

Soumya‚Äî Krishnadasa, we will go in advance and get ready the hospitalities due to a guest. Bring up the gentleman.

(Exeunt Soumya and Meenanka).

Dhruva.‚Äî Uncle, is everybody doing well in the city and the country?

Sumati‚Äî All are happy, except your parents.

Dhruva.‚Äî They are alive, I hope.

Sumati.‚Äî They live, but are plunged in an ocean of grief.

Dhruva.‚Äî The bondage of desire rules the mind, and leads it to destruction, by binding it to the objects of sense. Sorrow and joy are alike dispensed by Lakshmi’s Lord. It is He that sends us everything.

**Sumati‚Äî**If you go with me, universal bliss will follow.

Sumati‚Äî Your separation is the cause.

Dhruva ‚Äî Let my father think that he never saw me.

Sumati.‚Äî Is this the reply also to the mother’s grief ?

**Sumati.‚Äî**You do not realize what a mother’s affection means.

Prathoodara.‚Äî No debtor repays a debt withoutdifficulty. If a suit be filed in a court of

** ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡••

** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§≠‡•á, ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§®‡•Ç‡§§‡§®‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•ã ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§¶‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§¶‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§∑‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ö‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§•‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§∞‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§Ç‡••

justice, one has to guard the doorway ofpleaders for a full year. Then the judgesrefuse to award the compound interest whichis our profit. So I have given up money-lending.

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**Trade in grain is equally bad. Theprice of grain has greatly fallen in the market. There is neither seller nor buyer.

Prathoodara.‚Äî Then what is being done now? Letbrother-in-law take me as a partner withequal share in something or other.

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**Recently I began a new trade ingold and rubies. They say that there willbe great profit in it.

Prathoodara.‚Äî So also, fear of king’s punishment.It is only by theft of what is rubbed on thetouchstone, and by receipt of jewels producedby thieves, that profit has to be derived.

‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§®‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç‡•• ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§õ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡••

**‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§É‡•§ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§Ø‡§É‡•• ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç‡•• ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡•§

‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§π‡§Ç‡§§, ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É ‡§™‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•• ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§•‡§ø ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≤‡•ã ‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡§ï‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§É‡•§ ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§π‡••

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É ‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø) (‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡•§)

‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡••

‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡•á ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡••

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**That is a trade-secret derived from tradition. What is the good of mentioning it? If you wish, be my partner in this business.

Prathoodara.‚Äî This is no trading but only cheating: but as it is enjoined by honoured custom, it must be followed. Be it so; I will contribute my share of capital.

Bhanumati.‚Äî O, joy ! I think that our contract is very auspicious. See, on the road, goes a certain rustic with a long beard. In his hand see a necklace with dazzling gems set therein. Call him here.

(Prathoodara does as bidden). (Enters, forester, holding a necklace in hand).

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**Friend, Is the necklace for sale ?

Forester.‚Äî I shall give it if a suitable price be got.

‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§∑‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø) ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ ‡§à‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§æ‡§ü‡§ï‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡••

‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É‚Äî (‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ) ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§π‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•á‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§® ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡•• ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§µ‡§£‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç‡•• ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡•§ (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•á‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø).

‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî ‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡••

Bhanumati.‚Äî I will examine it; hand it up (So takes it with both hands, and rubs it on the touchstone). Brother, the gold appears to be slightly impure. Observe on your touchstone.

Prathoodara.‚Äî (doing so). It seems so in my opinion too.

Forester.‚Äî At what value is this estimated?

Bhanumati.‚Äî If only there was not this dark line in the diamond, it would be simply invaluable. Sir, let this be in my box. After showing it to a few merchants, I will return it in the evening. Please call again. (So saying he puts it in a box).

Forester.‚Äî I will bring it in the evening. Let the necklace be returned.

** ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•§ ‡§® ‡§ï‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§É‡•§ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§

** ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡•• ‡§® ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡••

** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§¶‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••

** ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî**‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç‡•• ‡§π‡§æ ‡§π‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•Å‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞ ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡§§‡§ø)

Prathoodara.‚Äî Sir, there is no cause for suspicion. You may go.

Forester.‚Äî You better give up the necklace. I won’t leave without it.

Bhanumati.‚Äî Which necklace?

Forester.‚Äî The one handed by me just now.

Bhanumati.‚Äî When given and into whose hand?

Forester.‚Äî What is this a piece of city ‚Äî fraud? Alas! Alas! the merchant has stolen a necklace. Help! Help! (So he cries).

Then enters the town guard policeman.

** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§â‡§™‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡••

(‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§Ø‡§•‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡•§)

‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡••‡§ö‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

Policeman.‚Äî Sirrah, merchant, where is the necklace?

Bhanumati.‚Äî I saw no necklace at all.

Forester.‚Äî Sir, search this box.

Policeman.‚Äî Fellow, show the box.

Bhanumati.‚Äî Let your honour sit down. I will state the matter.

Policeman.‚Äî Give up the necklace into my hands. Then state the matter.

Bhanumati.‚Äî (does as ordered). Let your honour, zealous in the discharge of public duties, inquire into the matter as to how he got it. It must be a stolen article.

Forester.‚Äî Not so. I brought good news to the king from his son in the forest. Being

** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç, ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ö‡•Ä‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡•• ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡••

**Policeman.‚Äî**This is improbable, but all three of you are thieves. Let us go to the Police station. There, when the needle-torture is inflicted, truth discloses itself.

**Prathoodara.‚Äî**What is it that I did? belong to this shop. I do not

**Policeman.‚Äî**I am certain that you have both abetted this theft. So both of you should go (to the station).

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**What is the good of going there? Let the necklace be shared by us.

** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§É‚Äî‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§É‡••
** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç (‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø).
** ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡••
** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§≠‡§ü‡•á‡§® ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••
** ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç‡•§
** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ï‡§Ç‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡§°‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§ü‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É‡••
** ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡••
** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§§‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§®‡•á‡§®‡••

(‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ö‡§∞‡§æ‡§É)

~~

~~

Policeman.‚Äî Let a half share be given to me.

**Bhanumati.‚Äî**Be it so. (So gives).

Forester.‚Äî What is this injustice?

Policeman.‚Äî What is the injustice? The King’s property is taken by the King’s servant.

Forester.‚Äî I shall go and inform the King.

Policeman.‚Äî Take this 100 Rs. If you reveal this, imprisonment will be the consequence to you. Such is the law in cities.

Forester.‚ÄîLet something more be paid.

Policeman.‚Äî Verily, a pile of hundred Rupees is what has never been heard of or seen by you. Let it be accepted quietly. (Exent merchants and forester).

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ü‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§≠‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§É)‡•§

** ‡§≠‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ø, ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ø‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§≠‡§ü‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡•Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§Ö‡§≤‡§Ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Ç‡••

** ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‚Äî** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡••

Enter another policeman with a toss of the curtain.

Another Policeman.‚Äî Friend, be quick, be quick. Dhruva, heir apparent to the throne, makes entry into the town. The royal command is that all the Police should be alert in uni- form in their posts of duty.

Exeunt.

ACT V. SCENE IV.

Palace. Enter King - Suruchi, Dhruva, Narada, Suneeti, and Sumati.

Narada.‚Äî OKing, receive the jewel of an heir-apparent, who is a prominent Bhakta of Narayana, a favourite of fortune, and a boy of great spiritual merit. Become blessed by this.

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî** ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡••

** ‡§ß‡•Å‡§µ‡§É‚Äî**(‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø)

**‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ï‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Æ
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ú‡§≤‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§≠‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§Ç

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

**‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§ø‡§®‡§ö‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ ‡§ö ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ **

King.‚Äî I am greatly obliged by the gift of the sage, for, my son is virtually born again.

Dhruva.‚Äî (Prostrating before Suruchi).

The lesson that you (mother) taught me by considering me unfit to set foot on this throne of the King without first worshipping the lotus-feet of Krishna venerated by Pranesa, has been a blessing attended with spiritual merit. I therefore first prostrate at your feet as those of my preceptor, a stepmother’s though they:be.

Suruchi.‚Äî God be thanked that you, a mere child as you are, have returned safe after a journey

** ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‚Äî**

‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ç‡§ï‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§≤‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§≠‡§•‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡•§

in the woods, to save me and confer joy on your mother and father, at last. Accursed me, that I spoke harsh words without sense. As you happened to be a boy of meritorious spirituality, a pious faith resulted, as if from my random words.

Dhruva‚Äî(Prostrating to father).

My father, pardon the boy who being easily offended, abandoned you his own father, for a long time, in order to promote his own pleasure. The pang that resulted to you on my account cursed Dhruva (me) in such a way that moksha was not obtained (by him) in spite of the direct interview he had with Lakshmi’s Lord.

King‚Äî Darling! having wished to ascend the region of my lap, just for a moment, and failed in

** ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§É ‚Äî** ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**(‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§¨‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•á) (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç)

the attempt, you have soared to the exalted height of Dhruva’s planet, there to reign till the very end of a cycle of time (Kalpa). Ojoy! blessed indeed am I, my good son, that I have beheld here your lovely face, with eyes suffused with tears of joy. That I, a father, have been excelled by my own son, is just as it should be.

Dhruva.‚Äî (Prostrating before his mother Suneeti). Mother, for a long time to come, I will not part from the nursing shelter of your hands. In the jungle, it was your ambrosial blessing that always shielded me (from danger).

Mother, living with me and the King, quite easy in mind, there will be no occasion at all hereafter for you to wash your hands with tears.

(Suneeti embracing her darling over and over again

said nothing).

(To herself).

At first a residence in the forest, away from the husband and neglected by him,‚Äî then, the birth of this boy preceded by an eating of the seed, (then) his journey to the forest and return,‚Äî recollecting all this, and now, being face to face with Dhruva my son of beautiful form, I feel engulfed in an ocean of ecstasy,‚Äî my bosom filled with mother’s milk pouring it out, because of maternal tenderness.

Narada.‚ÄîDhruva, come (here).

I will at once seat you on the lap of the King, as on that account, you grieved in the forest, suffering from humiliation.

(does as stated),

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî**

**‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á
‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡••‡•®‡•©‡•Ø‡•• **

**Sumati.‚Äî**Triumph! Triumph! Oworld-ruling monarch, with a blessed son and virtuous wives; may an uninterrupted shower of fortune fall on your head in plenty.

King.‚Äî Verily, a family that had lost its lustre, has been saved from grief. O Sumati, you are pre-eminent among ministers. In fact, the service rendered by you is quite immeasurable.

Sumati.‚Äî The world congratulates you on your fortune, O King of wonderful merit. As for me, to serve you is my duty, a servant and brother-in-law as I am.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡•§
‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•®‡•™‡•¶‡••

** ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‚Äî** ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ü‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••

** ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‚Äî**

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§∂‡§™‡•Ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¨‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§É
‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç‡••‡•®‡•™‡•ß‡••

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

King.‚Äî Let gold and gems be distributed to all good men, according to desert. Let all good men rejoice, for conducing to the well-being of the heir-apparent.

**Sumati.‚Äî**As your majesty commands.

Narada.‚Äî May the Lord, whose feet are adored by the Lord of the Pranas,- who is worshipped by Lakshmi, who bestows salvation on the faithful, who is an ocean of grace, and who begot Bramha from his navel, confer blessings on all.
